  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_94793355-ed96-4925-a17c-a975168105c0'
      });

Desperate to save Lia's life, her erstwhile assassin, Kaden, has told the Vendan Komizar that she has the gift, and the Komizar's interest in Lia is greater than anyone could have foreseen.<br /><br />Meanwhile, nothing is straightforward: There's Rafe, who lied to Lia but has sacrificed his freedom to protect her; Kaden, who meant to assassinate her but has now saved her life; and the Vendans, whom Lia always believed to be savages. Now that she lives among them, however, she realizes that may be far from the truth. Wrestling with her upbringing, her gift, and her sense of self, Lia must make powerful choices that will affect her country... and her own destiny.</span>

I cannot wait for what I'm sure will be a breathtaking finale.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8518444551420876360">well well well. what a pleasant surprise. this is better than the first book and i couldnt be more grateful or relieved.<br/><br/>i will say this is still an 'in the moment' kind of story. i felt much more present and engaged whilst reading this (compared to <i>‘kiss of deception'</i>), but i still dont think this story/series is going to have a long-lasting effect on me.<br/><br/>i like the character development that is present in this and how its evolved from a silly love triangle. the new characters are good additions,</span>
  <span id="freeText8518444551420876360" style="display:none">well well well. what a pleasant surprise. this is better than the first book and i couldnt be more grateful or relieved.<br /><br />i will say this is still an 'in the moment' kind of story. i felt much more present and engaged whilst reading this (compared to <i>‘kiss of deception'</i>), but i still dont think this story/series is going to have a long-lasting effect on me.<br /><br />i like the character development that is present in this and how its evolved from a silly love triangle. the new characters are good additions, but rafe and kaden are still my boys. the writing itself seems improved, but the pacing is still kinda slow and the story a little uneventful. the concept of people with gifts is interesting, but is still unexplained/unexplored, which is a bummer. <br /><br />so some good and some bad. decent entertainment for what it is and a lot more interesting than the first book!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1032150880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12968146465335588381"><strong>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/07/blog-tour-and-giveaway-heart-of.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Win a copy of <i>The Heart of Betrayal</i>!</a>***</strong><br/><br/>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/06/review-heart-of-betrayal-by-mary-e.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>The Heart of Betrayal by Mary E. Pearson<br/>Book Two of the Remnant Chronicles<br/>Publisher: Henry Holt and Co. (BYR)<br/>Publication Date: July 7, 2015<br/>Rating: 4 stars<br/>Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>Intrigue abounds in this hotly anticipated sequel to The Kiss of Deception!<br/><br/>Held captive in the barbarian kingdom of Venda, Lia and Rafe have little chance of escape. Desperate to save her life, Lia's</span>
  <span id="freeText12968146465335588381" style="display:none"><strong>***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/07/blog-tour-and-giveaway-heart-of.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Win a copy of <i>The Heart of Betrayal</i>!</a>***</strong><br /><br />***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/06/review-heart-of-betrayal-by-mary-e.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />The Heart of Betrayal by Mary E. Pearson<br />Book Two of the Remnant Chronicles<br />Publisher: Henry Holt and Co. (BYR)<br />Publication Date: July 7, 2015<br />Rating: 4 stars<br />Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />Intrigue abounds in this hotly anticipated sequel to The Kiss of Deception!<br /><br />Held captive in the barbarian kingdom of Venda, Lia and Rafe have little chance of escape. Desperate to save her life, Lia's erstwhile assassin, Kaden, has told the Vendan Komizar that she has the gift, and the Komizar's interest in Lia is greater than anyone could have foreseen.<br /><br />Meanwhile, nothing is straightforward: there's Rafe, who lied to Lia, but has sacrificed his freedom to protect her; Kaden, who meant to assassinate her but has now saved her life; and the Vendans, whom Lia always believed to be barbarians. Now that she lives amongst them, however, she realizes that may be far from the truth. Wrestling with her upbringing, her gift, and her sense of self, Lia must make powerful choices that will affect her country... and her own destiny.<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />I'm half-tempted to just leave this review saying, "GO READ THIS SERIES NOW". Seriously, the struggle of writing a review for a book you really, really enjoyed. This book is super close to five stars - The Kiss of Deception was a five-star read for me - but it came just a wee bit short. Still, I LOVED this book. I cannot wait to read book three.<br /><br />In this novel, Lia and Rafe are taken to Venda to live at the mercy of the Komizar. Lia has no allies in Venda, though she starts to build small alliances with unexpected citizens. There is something about Venda that is unlike anything Lia has experienced. Her gift changes and starts taken shape. Lia begins to see things in Venda that she has n seen before. All the while, Lia has drawn the Komizar's interest, and not a good interest. Rafe lies his way into staying alive, with everyone believing that he is the Royal Emissary of the Dalbreck crown prince. With each passing day, it is clear that there are no rules to survival, and both must do what they can to have a chance at escaping. <br /><br />I had a bad feeling about this book, initially. We're on Kaden's home turf, which led me to believe that the love triangle would grow more strong, fueling Kaden's feelings for Lia, and possibly having Lia develop deep for Kaden. Sorry, Kaden fans. The romance isn't straight and clear-cut, but it's no longer a love triangle. Lia uses Kaden to survive, and while she feels guilty, she doesn't feel love. There are no rules to survival.<br /><br />Continuing on the vein of the romance. It seems like EVERYONE is in love (or in lust) with Lia. The Komizar is around Lia, Kaden, and Rafe's age, and he becomes interested in her too. But his interest is more in power - the Vendan people begin to see Lia as a divine sign of some sort (because of her gift), and Lia works hard to build a good reputation and relationship with the people. So we have the Komizar, Kaden, and Rafe all vying for Lia's hand.<br /><br />Of course, the Komizar has zero shot (he's the villain - or one of them). In my opinion, Kaden NEVER had a shot (not even in The Kiss of Deception), but that's just my opinion. In this book, it becomes very, very clear who Lia has feelings for, who Lia cares about, etc. It's stated in her thoughts, how she loves one and how she cares for one. Two totally different emotions going on, and Kaden is not on the receiving end of the emotion he wants. I believe Kaden truly loves her, but it seems like a blind love. Honestly, Kaden's feelings for Lia seem more like obsession or fascination. And Lia... she cares about him, but not like that.<br /><br />Rafe. Oh, Rafe. I loved Rafe in The Kiss of Deception (I think I was one of the few that knew prince from assassin), and I love him even more in this book. Both he and Lia do terrible things to survive, to fight for each other, to keep each other alive - especially Lia. Rafe has a good heart, but he is also fierce and clever, calculating and, well, a bit impulsive. He and Lia both don't have patience. Rafe could chop up Kaden in a heartbeat, but he never does. He's smart like that.<br /><br />I don't really feel much for Kaden, if you didn't notice. We get a lot of backstory in this book for Kaden (and the Komizar, too), but I don't really care all that much about Kaden (or the Komizar). I'd love to push Kaden towards Calantha, or Pauline. <br /><br />So, in my opinion, the love triangle (or potential love triangle, however you saw it in The Kiss of Deception) is pretty much resolved in this book. The emotional romance is pretty clear-cut in this book. There are some things that made my heart ache for Lia, but once you read the book, you'll get it. I respect her for all of her decisions.<br /><br />The romance between Rafe and Lia heats up in this book. Lia is still angry at Rafe for deceiving, and Rafe is angry for the same reason, and there is plenty of tension between them. But at the same time, they both care about each other, and fell in love with each other, and fall in love with each other all over again. Imprisoned, forced to play roles and deceive everyone and act like they hate each other - and yet, they still fall deeper for each other. It's sweet! And sizzling. Wink.<br /><br />On to the story, sans romance! I feel like not much occurred in this book, in terms of the war and such. Venda has been massacring enemy camps and soldiers, killing many and taking supplies. It's awful, and in my opinion, hard to feel sorry for Venda. I do, but I don't. It's obvious that Pearson wants readers to fall in love with Venda - she spent so much page time describing Venda, having Lia convinced that it's not all bad, etc. I wasn't really buying it, but then, I don't really care for Venda or Kaden. I'm more curious about Dalbreck.<br /><br />Venda is like a bubble, and Lia and Rafe don't really know what is happening outside of Venda. Short snippets of news might pass around, but the war and policies and declarations aren't made known often. So, in my opinion, the SERIES plot was slow. The book's plot mostly focused on Lia and her relationships with the Vendan people, the Komizar, Kaden, and Rafe. A lot with Rafe.<br /><br />I like the mysterious "gift" part of the series plot though. A lot of it revolves around Venda, curiously. And yet, I feel more lost, in terms of Lia's gift, and its connection to Venda. Hopefully all will be explained in book three.<br /><br />Book three! I need it! The ending of this one wasn't TOO cliffhanger-like, but it makes me anxious. Not for Lia and Rafe, but for the kingdoms. I actually like the ending (I think), though the fact that there are so many perspectives (since The Kiss of Deception though) makes me wonder if the author is going to pull a Veronica Roth...<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />I wish things Lia had to do didn't have to happen. It's not like in A Court of Thorns and Roses, between Rhysand and Feyre (sexual assault, rape, anyone? How in the world is anyone finding Rhysand sexy?!), so no worries about that. But I wish things were different! Of course, there are no rules to survival.<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />Anyway. YES. I would totally recommend this series in general. This sequel novel is great! I loved The Kiss of Deception, and I really enjoyed this book. Now, as long as the love triangle is officially dead and Rafe and Lia can ride off into the sunset from start to finish of book three (that might be an exaggeration)... I'll be happy. Maybe. Perhaps I want Venda to burn a little too. And maybe Morrighan too.<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4.5 stars -&gt; rounded down to 4 stars (for a reason I can't say without spoiling things!). Overall, I'm really pleased with this book, especially with the romance. I definitely want to see more from the series plot (and not just the romance - stop pushing the triangle, Pearson!), so hopefully there will be an epic showdown in book three! I have a feeling that Pearson will take us to Dalbreck - finally!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12968146465335588381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

</a><br><br>Lia's still her fierce self, not particularly skilled at anything but cunning as all get out. She does, however, pull off an impressive feat with cards, thanks to her brothers.<br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-0dqJCxW6y_o/VScTqHbceYI/AAAAAAAAW-I/LySFW9cZwKM/s1600/ferb_fletcher__card_shark__animated__by_jaycasey-d5bivg6.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>There were moments when I wasn't sure if she was toying with someone, playing a game...or if she was really sincere. Reading to find out how her strategizing and manipulating fared left me on the edge of my seat for much of the book.<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-svSvvzG8zHM/VSbPWPqbEjI/AAAAAAAAW70/TYDfb2TxCzw/s1600/seriousreading.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Just when things finally seemed to be going her way -- if that's ever really possible when you're a hostage in a foreign land -- <i>someone</i> gets a crazy idea in his head that just might seal her fate.<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-JlNOl-XfOOk/VSbOttMMe6I/AAAAAAAAW7k/PPe9p3Iz3OI/s1600/whaaaattt.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428671137ra/14463682.gif" height="172" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><div>
<br>As I read on, I started getting inklings of another truth yet to be uncovered, especially from two particular points of view. (You remember how there were so many perspectives in the first book. Samesies in this one.) It all started to come together, the pieces fitting together just right, and I couldn't believe I hadn't guessed the truth of it before...or at least parts of it.<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-e6c7R8bdLpU/VSbgBk_d6aI/AAAAAAAAW9c/_7bn8iH5TZA/s1600/aha.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428671137ra/14463683.gif" height="184" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>&lt;<br><br>As far as the romance goes, I still maintain that it's not a love triangle, even though there are now three, yes <i>three</i>, men vying for Lia's affections...sort of. I can't say any more without worry of spoilers. But to <i>me</i>, it's clear with whom Lia's heart lies. It was the same for me in the first book, too, though.<br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-epFltFujmEQ/VSbaUK6wrgI/AAAAAAAAW8k/tz5Ou2dg1Ns/s1600/godownwithship.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428671137ra/14463684.gif" height="140" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>There's loads more kissing than I expected, not that I'm complaining.<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-ld0Dd-DTYro/VSbbUHjc4pI/AAAAAAAAW8s/pJ16rFANMEs/s1600/kiss.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428671137ra/14463685.gif" height="136" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>Some that made me do this:<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-sl0sf7Dh0LI/VSbbqGCgE0I/AAAAAAAAW80/aTOX17UCsbM/s1600/swooning.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428671137ra/14463686.gif" height="135" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>And some that made me sad...<br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-CLTK3ndo5wA/VSbb9kMApCI/AAAAAAAAW88/qUKawJxRW_c/s1600/brokenheartsad.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428671137ra/14463687.gif" height="156" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>And some that just made me plain mad.<br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-wWwu18C9MxM/VSbcHYchNnI/AAAAAAAAW9E/l0-_vPcrOl8/s1600/ragingdarla.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428671137ra/14463688.gif" height="177" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>Then I started getting really angry as what was happening in Venda began to have repercussions outside of the kingdom walls.<br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-K434Kf07BLk/VScV7OvKS0I/AAAAAAAAW-c/iFZPTA6OOks/s1600/tumblr_ndafnhZRr91tq4of6o1_400.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428671137ra/14463689.gif" height="180" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>But don't think that Lia is going to sit idly by and watch as things unfold. She's a woman of action, as we've already seen. And she may not have an entourage, but she has help.<br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-xUEPzSpMHi0/VSbhNSY7AJI/AAAAAAAAW9k/J6bp1VR2yhY/s1600/savetheprincess.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428671137ra/14463690.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>The entire book was extremely intense, but that last quarter had me turning those pages so damn fast!<br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-A40y4QQP8Ig/VSbiNNhxrmI/AAAAAAAAW94/crJal1WJIgg/s1600/fastreading.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428671137ra/14463691.gif" height="135" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>I didn't want it to be over yet. :( But that end...that end, yo!<br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-pvOeR2TYEhM/VSbMe5iNgeI/AAAAAAAAW7Y/SZ_IfPuGkQA/s1600/brbdying.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428671137ra/14463692.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>I will do my best to write a full, coherent review closer to the book's release date, but that's the beauty of these posts. I can get those feelings out now, in hopes of doing just that.<br><br>The fact of the matter remains:  this book was an<br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-xWb0YEeevns/VSbhsTI2tJI/AAAAAAAAW9w/Q4YN-VjZqM4/s1600/emotionalrollercoaster.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428671137ra/14463693.gif" height="135" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>And one hell of a thrill ride. I am already dying for the next book!</div></span>
  <a data-text-id="165380477114145201" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1099135444" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1099135444" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5789353-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605042512p2/5789353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1099135444?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/5789353-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=from-publishers">from-publishers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=age-young-adult">age-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-dystopia">genre-dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=requested-for-review">requested-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-romance">genre-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=arc-physical">arc-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-action-adventure">genre-action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=bought-online">bought-online</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1099135444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2264434988598233648">An Advanced Reader Copy was provided by the publisher for review.<br/><br/>This sequel ripped me apart and put me back together again. I was constantly wondering what other twist and turn was going to happen, which person should they trust. And what exactly was going on between the political parties between the kingdoms. I loved that this was set in Venda for we get to see another kingdom that doesn't rely on its resources but on its leader. Even if that leader happens to be the Komizar. Chapters are shor</span>
  <span id="freeText2264434988598233648" style="display:none">An Advanced Reader Copy was provided by the publisher for review.<br /><br />This sequel ripped me apart and put me back together again. I was constantly wondering what other twist and turn was going to happen, which person should they trust. And what exactly was going on between the political parties between the kingdoms. I loved that this was set in Venda for we get to see another kingdom that doesn't rely on its resources but on its leader. Even if that leader happens to be the Komizar. Chapters are short so don't worry about this being an extended read. It looks like a massive read, but it's really not. I practically flew through the pages and savoured it until the end. I didn't want it to end. There isn't a whole lot of focus on romance and I was glad to see more of a political back-story than anything. Being part of the enemy camp can't be easy but Lia manages to stay and even accept the people.<br /><br />As for the characters, Lia has definitely grown a bit more. Maybe seeing more of the world can do that to a princess. Being more open to another culture even if it's known to be a barbaric one. I liked that she saw more of the people and observed their daily lives. They live in a harsh climate and their resources are more limited than other kingdoms so to see her finally accept them shows so much growth for her character. There's a point in the book where I thought the Komizar could be something he wasn't.. But as I read on, I was sadly mistaken. What I did want to see was more of a certain Prince and he was there but I didn't really get to feel too much about what he was feeling. It was more of him being the hero and trying to save her every single time. *rolls eyes*<br /><br />Then there's the ending which abruptly killed me and I haven't been able to recover since. I just know things aren't going down that path but for Mary E. Pearson to put us through that torture ahhhhh... Such a crazy ending that's for sure. I was waiting for it to be climatic!<br /><br />A strong sequel, The Heart of Betrayal will have you wanting more of Lia's world as she navigates a savage country. Will she lose herself or will she find a way to escape? Just read it and you'll find out.<br /><br />RATING 5/5<br /><br />QUOTES<br /><br />"I came for you, Lia, no matter who or what you are, and I don't care what mistakes I made or what mistakes you made. I'd make every single one again, if that was the only way to be with you." (28)<br /><br />"Sometimes winning is not only a matter of knowing the rules, but of making your opponent think he knows them better." (202)<br /><br />"Stop telling me what to do or say! Um tired of everyone trying to control every word out of my mouth." (280)<br /><br />"Betrayal by ones own kind is a wound that never heals." (323)<br /><br />"I don't play games. I wage wars. Don't make me safe one on you." (357)<br /><br />"We've had a terrible start—it doesn't mean we can't have a better ending." (439)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2264434988598233648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1278130612" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278130612" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1278130612?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=mature-ya">mature-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1278130612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15488812244945437439">If you weren't a fan of the first book (<i>and some of my friends were not</i>), then I don't think anything about this book is going to change your mind. Sorry.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441562733ra/16123541.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Buuuut...</b><br/>If you've been chomping at the bit (<i>because maybe you're a horse?</i>) to find out what happened to Lia, Raffe, & Kaden once they got inside the walls of Venda? Then I think you'll be pretty happy with Pearson's book. Secrets, magic, prophesies, and (<i>as the title suggests</i>) betrayal! Good stuff.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441562624ra/16123534.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Best part of the book for me? <br/><b>The Heart of Bet</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15488812244945437439" style="display:none">If you weren't a fan of the first book (<i>and some of my friends were not</i>), then I don't think anything about this book is going to change your mind. Sorry.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441562733ra/16123541.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Buuuut...</b><br>If you've been chomping at the bit (<i>because maybe you're a horse?</i>) to find out what happened to Lia, Raffe, &amp; Kaden once they got inside the walls of Venda? Then I think you'll be pretty happy with Pearson's book. Secrets, magic, prophesies, and (<i>as the title suggests</i>) betrayal! Good stuff.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441562624ra/16123534.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Best part of the book for me? <br><b>The Heart of Betrayal</b> is exactly what I hoped it would be, in that the non-love-triangle-<i>triangle</i> didn't morph into a real <b>
  <i>Triangle</i>
</b>. Sure, Kaden is still in love with Lia, but she doesn't return anything but friendship. There's none of that wishy-washy Who-Do-I-Really-Love shit happening here.<br>It's Raffe. Boom! End of discussion.<br><i>Kaden can just keep on pining...</i><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441562624ra/16123535.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And why <i>should</i> she have feelings for Kaden? I mean, Raffe is putting his ass on the line to save her, and, meanwhile, Kaden has turned her over to his evil boss! Sure, he's hoping he can protect her, but I'm not sure why he thinks that would make him her <i>go-to</i> guy for romance.<br><i>Psssht. Men.</i><br>However! After finding out more of his backstory, I'm definitely hoping he gets a HEA. Poor guy. That sob story got me right in the feels, and I can see why the fella might have a few issues.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441562733ra/16123542.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alrighty, I do have one complaint...<br>Pearson didn't do the <i>bestest</i> job recapping what happened in the last book. Some authors are better than others when it comes to this, and I'm afraid that Pearson isn't one of the good ones.<br>Now, I know a lot of you out there probably reread the previous books <i>before</i> you crack open the brand new ones. But I read a shitload of books each year, and simply <i>don't have the <b>time</b></i> to do that. And while I may remember the general theme of most books, after a year or so, I just can't remember the details. I tend to rely on the authors to give my mind a <s>hard shove</s> gentle nudge when I'm reading books that are part of a series. And, honestly, that wasn't very well done here. I was still trying to play catch-up right till the end.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441563033ra/16123571.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I said that to say <i>this</i>: if you don't have a stellar memory for details, then you may want to go ahead and do a reread before picking this one up. <br>Oh, and watch out for that CLIFFHANGER at the end!<br><i>
  <b>Dear God, Pearson! Are you trying to give me a heart attack, woman?!</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441563033ra/16123572.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><div>
  <a href="http://www.addicted2heroines.com/2015/09/review-heart-of-betrayal-remnant.html" title="Addicted 2 Heroines" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412937777i/11444542.jpg" alt="Addicted 2 Heroines" width="100%" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div></span>

<div id="review_1895851972" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1895851972" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1895851972?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/25851812-the-heart-of-betrayal">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1895851972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12034040507822607852"><b>“Because with my last dying breath, I would make him regret the day he ever laid eyes on me.”</b><br/><br/>•I'm still unsure <b>whether I should consider this series as guilty pleasure or not</b>; I still haven't been able to peg it. It's as if it lives in this sort of limbo, where you have this astonishingly <b>intelligent writing and world-building</b> on one hand, and <b> tons of ya tropes</b> on the other, love triangle included. And the more I think about it, the more I realize I actually like the in-between sort of story th</span>
  <span id="freeText12034040507822607852" style="display:none"><b>“Because with my last dying breath, I would make him regret the day he ever laid eyes on me.”</b><br /><br />•I'm still unsure <b>whether I should consider this series as guilty pleasure or not</b>; I still haven't been able to peg it. It's as if it lives in this sort of limbo, where you have this astonishingly <b>intelligent writing and world-building</b> on one hand, and <b> tons of ya tropes</b> on the other, love triangle included. And the more I think about it, the more I realize I actually like the in-between sort of story that came out of it. It's precisely the kind of book I would look for if I simply wanted to relax and think of nothing for a few days, without ending up banging my head against a wall in an attempt to forget the horror I just read. In this sense, the Remnant Chronicles are the perfect series.<br /><br />•I like <b>Lia</b> more and more with each page I read. She's <b>fierce</b>, <b>steadfast</b>; in my language, there's an idiom we use for stubborn and determined people who would do just anything to get want they want, who are said "not to look anybody in the face". So here, in my head Lia is the perfect example of someone who never looks anybody in the face. She knows where she needs to get and what she needs to do, and she complies without complaints or self-pity. I think her attitude in this book is<b> worthy of admiration</b>, and I was honestly happy with her as a character, in general. However, I still don't see why everyone should love her on the spot; I get that the people of Venda revere her because of the prophecy, but that makes the character look only like the umpteenth <b>clean and tidy, all-too-good, perfect and shiny chosen one</b>. That was really irritating, considering that the one actual thing that Lia does for this people is recite some poetry and prayers. If that's where the story's going, I would like to see her actually <i>act</i> in the next book.<br /><br />•<b>The love triangle</b> is, surprisingly, not as heavy as one may think, even though it's undeniably there and at times it really is felt. For what it's worth, I think it's well handled. Besides, both Rafe and Kaden are way too likeable <s>and hot</s> not to fall for them. I think Rafe could be explored with more depth, while Kaden satisfied me more in this respect. <br /><br />•<b>The Komizar</b> proved to be far more interesting that I'd have thought, <b>ruthless</b>, <b>insidious</b>, <b>cunning</b> and utterly <b>cold-blooded</b>; maybe I would have liked him to be a bit more unpredictable -two or three chapters with him are more than enough to figure his character out perfectly. I do hope he'll return in the final instalment and show more sides of himself. <br /><br />•<b>I was never bored</b>, not for one second, but I should probably mention that <b>the whole plot revolves around mind games and politics</b>, therefore you'd better brace yourself if you're more of an adrenaline junkie. Moreover, even though I didn't perceive it as a flaw while I was reading it, objectively the book does suffer from a mild form of middle book syndrome -the major events are very few because the whole story takes place at the Vendan court.<br /><br />➽ <i>The Heart of Betrayal</i> undoubtedly is <b>a worthy sequel</b> to <i>The Kiss of Deception</i>, and its strengths certainly exceed its weaknesses. With a few focused improvements, the next book will mathematically make for a great conclusion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12034040507822607852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1917598694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1917598694" />
    <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net"><img alt="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390032p2/7971097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1917598694?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net">Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net?shelf=cover-porn">cover-porn</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1917598694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13883223664478568656"><i>See this review and more on:</i> <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bookbastion.net'>www.bookbastion.net</a><br/>___________________<br/><br/><b>This one might win the award for toughest review of 2017. </b><br/><br/>You might remember my earlier review for the first book in the series: The Kiss of Deception, which I loved and showered praise on. While I was really excited to crack into this one, and still really enjoyed it, I felt a little let down.<br/><br/>One of the biggest disappointments to me in this book revolved around the situation Lia found herself in. "But Bentley," you say, "isn't t</span>
  <span id="freeText13883223664478568656" style="display:none"><i>See this review and more on:</i> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookbastion.net">www.bookbastion.net</a><br>___________________<br><br><b>This one might win the award for toughest review of 2017. </b><br><br>You might remember my earlier review for the first book in the series: The Kiss of Deception, which I loved and showered praise on. While I was really excited to crack into this one, and still really enjoyed it, I felt a little let down.<br><br>One of the biggest disappointments to me in this book revolved around the situation Lia found herself in. "But Bentley," you say, "isn't that the point of conflict?" Well, yes, but in a way I feel like this book undoes a lot of what I really enjoyed most about the first. Take for example, that <b>dreaded love triangle</b> from book one that just won't quit. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440614951ra/15999831.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Lia had essentially made her choice at the end of book 1, and although I knew she would be in close proximity to her potential second love interest, I had hoped she'd moved past him. However, because of the danger of her situation this time around, it actually turns out to be safer for her to pretend to still be interested in this guy, which of course leads to sort of feelings on both ends.<br><br><b>So, in a way Lia loses that powerful agency she had in the first book in favor of prolonging the inevitable.</b> She's still extremely intelligent and driven as a character, which I love, but she's no longer making decisions for herself and for her own future. Instead, she feels trapped under the thumb of not one, not two, but three different men in this book, who all want to get into her pants. <br><br>During the earliest pages of this book, when I knew we were about to meet the Komizar I was literally sending up prayers that he would turn out to be either old or ugly, or a combination of both. Of course when he's introduced he's young, hungry and just as handsome as the other two men in Lia's life. You can pretty much guess where that storyline goes from page one. <b>A lot of my friends who read this book seemed to love the Komizar. I mostly hated him.</b> I felt like Lia was really hampered by her connection to him and cringed every time I realized he was going to be in a scene.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494553212ra/22727970.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It just felt a little bit tired to me. I wanted more exploration of Venda and more politicking between the kingdoms, but instead this sort of sophomore slumped for me into a romantic story set in a fantasy world. <br><br>I will give Mary Pearson the same commendation I awarded her for the first book. <b>Her writing skills are top notch. She has a masterful command of prose and dialogue.</b> I feel like she's sort of unfairly categorized in Young Adult to be honest, when her prose seems a bit stronger than the typical books you'd find in the genre. I think she'd do quite well writing fantasy novels for adults at some point in her career. <br><br><b>I don't mean to sound like I hated this book - on the contrary, it was still quite engaging. I did enjoy learning more about Venda, and exploring all its hidden secrets alongside Lia.</b> I also took a shine to a few of the ancillary characters that Lia bumped into from time to time. There is a lot here still to love, and I am sure that this book was building up to some major events that are going to take place during the final installment. <br><br>I just hope book 3 moves past all the love triangle drama and really engages in the story I'm most interested in: Lia continuing her journey of self discovery both of her gift, and of her strengths as a woman who doesn't need to chain herself to a man in order to survive. <br><br>★★★★✰ = <b>4 out 5 stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13883223664478568656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1513258838" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1513258838?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1513258838" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7933660732872106757"><b>The Heart of Betrayal (The Remnant Chronicles #2), Mary E. Pearson</b><br/><br/>First of all, i loved the progression of the story in this book! <br/><br/>Held captive in the barbarian kingdom of Venda, Lia and Rafe have little chance of escape ... and even less of being together.<br/><br/>Desperate to save her life, Lia's erstwhile assassin, Kaden, has told the Vendan Komizar that she has a magical gift, and the Komizar's interest in Lia is greater than either Kaden or Lia foresaw.<br/><br/>Meanwhile, the foundations of Lia's deeply-held</span>
  <span id="freeText7933660732872106757" style="display:none"><b>The Heart of Betrayal (The Remnant Chronicles #2), Mary E. Pearson</b><br /><br />First of all, i loved the progression of the story in this book! <br /><br />Held captive in the barbarian kingdom of Venda, Lia and Rafe have little chance of escape ... and even less of being together.<br /><br />Desperate to save her life, Lia's erstwhile assassin, Kaden, has told the Vendan Komizar that she has a magical gift, and the Komizar's interest in Lia is greater than either Kaden or Lia foresaw.<br /><br />Meanwhile, the foundations of Lia's deeply-held beliefs are crumbling beneath her. Nothing is straightforward: there's Rafe, who lied to her, but has sacrificed his freedom to protect her; Kaden, who meant to assassinate her but has now saved her life; and the Vendans, whom she always believed to be barbarians but whom she now realizes are people who have been terribly brutalized by the kingdoms of Dalbreck and Morrighan. Wrestling with her upbringing, her gift, and her very sense of self, Lia will have to make powerful choices that affect her country, her people . . . and her own destiny.<br /><br />تاریخ خوانش روز پانزدهم ماه ژانویه سال 2017میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: قلب خائن: کتاب دوم سری تاریخهای باقیمانده؛ نویسنده: ماری ای پیرسون؛<br /><br />باورهای «لیا» در حال فروپاشی است؛ هیچ چیز سرراست نیست: «راف» به او دروغ گفته، اما برای حفظ او آزادی خود را فدا کرده است؛ «کادن» که قصد ترور او را داشته، جان او را نجات داده، و «وندانی»ها، که او همیشه باور داشت که آنها بربر هستند، اکنون متوجه شده آنها افرادی هستند که توسط پادشاهیهای «دالبرک» و «موریگان»، به طرز وحشیانه ای مورد خشونت قرار گرفته اند؛ «لیا» با خود مبارزه میکند، باید گزینشهایی انجام دهد، تا بر کشورش، و مردمانش، تأثیر بگذارد؛<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 14/08/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1238633962" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1238633962" />
    <a title="Chantal " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31668723-chantal"><img alt="Chantal " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464626501p2/31668723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1238633962?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal " href="/user/show/31668723-chantal">Chantal </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=published-2015">published-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1238633962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3590637365052338019"><b>2.5 stars</b> <br/><br/>It should be noted that I wasn't the biggest fan of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16429619.The_Kiss_of_Deception__The_Remnant_Chronicles___1_' title='The Kiss of Deception (The Remnant Chronicles, #1) by Mary E. Pearson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Kiss of Deception</a> but I found the ending so promising that I really wanted to give this series another chance.<br/><br/>If you loved <i>The Kiss of Deception</i>, don't let this review make you anxious, I'm pretty sure you will like this one more than the first. If you are like me however, and thought TKoD was very meh then this review is for you. To summarize: <b>I was hoping THoB would remedy many things I disliked in TKoD but that didn't happen un</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3590637365052338019" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b> <br /><br />It should be noted that I wasn't the biggest fan of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16429619.The_Kiss_of_Deception__The_Remnant_Chronicles___1_" title="The Kiss of Deception (The Remnant Chronicles, #1) by Mary E. Pearson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kiss of Deception</a> but I found the ending so promising that I really wanted to give this series another chance.<br /><br />If you loved <i>The Kiss of Deception</i>, don't let this review make you anxious, I'm pretty sure you will like this one more than the first. If you are like me however, and thought TKoD was very meh then this review is for you. To summarize: <b>I was hoping THoB would remedy many things I disliked in TKoD but that didn't happen unfortunately.</b><br /><br /><b>Warning: This review contains spoilers for the first instalment in the Remnant Chronicles series, <i>The Kiss of Deception</i>.</b><br /><br />When I picked up The Heart of Betrayal I had expectations (as you do with second instalments). <br /><br /><b>Expectation #1:</b> Lia, who is now being forced to enter Venda, will mature and develop as she has to learn to adapt to her new surroundings. Whatever the outcome, she will come out of it wiser and more patient.<br /><br /><b>→ Wrong.</b> In the first 10% of the book or so it actually seemed like this would happen. Lia kept her mouth shut and kept telling the reader how she was going to wait for the right moment before she acted. She kept saying how she was going to play the game better then everyone else. As you might guess, I was excited. I was thinking of what happened in The Winner’s Crime. Unfortunately, Lia doesn’t even come close to the calibre that is Kestrel. From that point onward, Lia actually seemed to regress, becoming her old, impulsive, reckless self. Now, I actually really liked Lia in the first book; there is nothing inherently wrong with a character being impulsive and a little reckless (as long as they aren’t stupid) BUT I need to see that a character learns from their mistakes and changes. Lia did neither.<br /><br /><b>Expectation #2:</b> The first novel was focused on the love triangle. It was all about boy issues and kissing. Surely, the second one will take a very different route; the romance will fade into the background as more interesting and important matters come into play.<br /><br /><b>→ Wrong.</b> This book still has entirely too much romance and entirely too little of everything else. How Lia still manages to expend so much brainpower on her men in this life and death situation is beyond me.<br /><br /><b>Expectation #3:</b> In the first book, Kaden and Rafe blended together for me. I didn’t care about either one. However, there is more opportunity in this one to make me choose one over the other. One of them (if not both) will grow on me. Kaden will show his badass side and actually become a man worthy of the title assassin.<br /><br /><b>→ Wrong.</b> The love triangle is worse than ever, I hated it even more than in the first book. I wanted to punch both Kaden and Rafe in the face. One says that in a good love triangle, the reader hops between love interests because they don’t know which one to choose. Well, this happened to me here. I truly couldn’t choose. Which one I disliked more.<br />I genuinely thought I would fall for Kaden because come on, he’s an assassin, I always seem to like the bad guys. He has to choose between the girl he loves and the loyalty to his kingdom. That’s romantic, right? Except that Kaden was so freaking gullible and weak-willed that he made me want to scream. He’s supposedly an incredibly skilled assassin. Apparently. I have yet to see proof of this. In this book, he is still just a boy who can’t do his job and is too busy making googly-eyes at Lia instead of seeing through her charade. Oh, and of course he has a tragic past that justifies all his actions. I sure didn't see that one coming. *rolls eyes*<br />Rafe was slightly better, at least he wasn’t as naive and pathetic as Kaden, but I still couldn’t get myself to like him. He kind of bored me, just like in the first book and he made some seriously stupid decisions all in the name of love.<br /><br /><b>Expectation #4:</b> What made TKoD a little more tolerable than some other YA fantasies was the fact that Lia wasn’t really a special snowflake. Yes, she is a princess but she is also a normal girl. Has flaws and supposedly doesn’t possess the gift. This notion will be maintained in the second book.<br /><br /><b>→ Wrong.</b> In this one, Lia becomes the most special of all special snowflakes. Both Kaden and Rafe love her with unwavering devotion and are willing to sacrifice everything for her even though they only met her a few months earlier. The people of Venda love Lia even though she is “enemy swine”. She is the one who has the gift and is prophesized to save the kingdoms. How original.<br /><br /><b>Expectation #5:</b> The plot is going too be more fast-paced and action-packed since Lia is now in enemy territory.<br /><br /><b>→ Not really.</b> The plot is slightly more exciting than in the first book (which really isn’t very difficult) but it still retains the meandering, slow-going quality. This isn’t always bad but in this case it felt like a let-down. The book should have been exciting and suspenseful but it wasn’t until the very end (much like TKoD).<br /><br /><b>Expectation #6:</b> We’re going to get more world-building and insight into the political system of the kingdoms.<br /><br /><b>→ Not really.</b> There are some well-written descriptions of Venda and how the kingdom works and we do get a tiny bit of politics. However, this is not enough for establishing an intricate political “chess game” or creating real suspense.<br /><br /><b>Expectation #7:</b> In this one, things will actually make sense.<br /><br /><b>→ Wrong.</b> I can’t say too much because of spoilers but some of the things that happen in this book are very unlikely and illogical. The way Lia gets through with everything she does. The way nobody ever questioned her motives. The fact that Rafe wasn’t found out. It just all seemed very convenient.<br /><br />Despite my very negative review, <i>The Heart of Betrayal</i> isn’t a terrible book. The writing is still quite lovely (though Mary E. Pearson overuses similes in my opinion), the plot overall is somewhat entertaining and Lia is still a character I can root for. The ending surprised me. However, I cannot say that I really liked this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3590637365052338019" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1026965857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1026965857" />
    <a title="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews"><img alt="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468898958p2/12502667.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1026965857?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" href="/user/show/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews">Rachel  (APCB Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews?shelf=exceeded-expectations">exceeded-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews?shelf=2015-standout">2015-standout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews?shelf=most-obsessed-favorites">most-obsessed-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews?shelf=fast-read">fast-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1026965857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15692630818001365426">Initial Review: OH MY GOSH THIS WAS PERFECT. The betrayal runs deep. Five Well-Deserved Stars from me! Review to come. <br/><br/>Read the full review @ <a href='http://aperfectioncalledbooks.blogspot.com/2015/06/arc-review-heart-of-betrayal-by-mary-e.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Perfection Called Books</a><br/><br/>Everyone fears second-book syndrome. I knew the minute I opened this book that I'd have nothing to fear. I was wildly impressed with the artful creation of The Kiss of Deception, and it's no surprise that The Heart of Betrayal captivated my heart as well.<br/><br/>I know many complain that The Kiss of Deception is slow. I urge you, if you fe</span>
  <span id="freeText15692630818001365426" style="display:none">Initial Review: OH MY GOSH THIS WAS PERFECT. The betrayal runs deep. Five Well-Deserved Stars from me! Review to come. <br /><br />Read the full review @ <a href="http://aperfectioncalledbooks.blogspot.com/2015/06/arc-review-heart-of-betrayal-by-mary-e.html" rel="nofollow noopener">A Perfection Called Books</a><br /><br />Everyone fears second-book syndrome. I knew the minute I opened this book that I'd have nothing to fear. I was wildly impressed with the artful creation of The Kiss of Deception, and it's no surprise that The Heart of Betrayal captivated my heart as well.<br /><br />I know many complain that The Kiss of Deception is slow. I urge you, if you feel that sentiment, to read this book. It's a definite change of pace (as in faster), and there's so much more going on. Picking up right after the end of The Kiss of Deception Lia is brought to a place that she's heard only horrifying things about. Slowly she realizes everything as not as it seems, and that the Komizar is more dangerous than she could ever imagine. As she struggles to keep her wits about her in this harsh court, she uncovers shocking truths and dares to fight back.<br /><br />If I had to describe this book in one word I think I'd use the word 'riveting.' I was so thoroughly engrossed in what was happening. We learn so much more about Venda and the culture. We delve deeper into each of these characters. Speaking of riveting, that Komizar! He's a bit Darkling-esque. He's power-hungry and vicious, yet he cares for his people. The complexity of his character was astounding, I loved it. Lia was fierce in this novel! She was her stubborn self and I loved her character growth. Rafe is perfection. That is all. We learn so much more about Kaden and his backstory. I liked him much better in this book. We also meet plenty of new, strong secondary characters.<br /><br />Pearson's writing continues to be beautiful and filled with twists and turns. Stellar world-building, superb plot development, brilliant plot twists, immense character growth, smoldering romance, I was highly impressed. The storyline was so intricate, yet it was weaved in a way that didn't seem too busy.<br /><br />The romance in this book was beyond spectacular. But first let me clarify something. This series does not contain a love triangle. Lia clearly favors one of them in the first book and sticks by her choice. It was such an immediate thing that someone who thinks this is a love triangle baffles me. That thought will be further crushed in The Heart of Betrayal. There are swoon-worthy moments and beautiful words exchanged. I was beaming and staring doe-eyed at the pages. No love triangle people, just love and I ship it!!<br /><br />I'm half mad, half enthusiastic and pleased that I decided to read this book now. I can push it on you all very early, yet now I have to wait forever until the next book. I enjoyed The Heart of Betrayal immensely, and it has surpassed my love of The Kiss of Deception. I recommend you give this one a try.<br /><br /><b>Was this review helpful? Vote for it on Amazon <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/customer-reviews/R2C7VPHJYDEJVM/ref=cm_cr_pr_rvw_ttl?ie=UTF8&amp;ASIN=0805099247" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15692630818001365426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219175103?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)" href="/user/show/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers">Alicia Batista (Addicted Readers)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=a-must-read">a-must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=i-dont-want-it-to-be-over">i-dont-want-it-to-be-over</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=amazing">amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=strong-female">strong-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=dual-pov">dual-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=soliders">soliders</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14564026-alicia-batista-addicted-readers?shelf=war">war</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219175103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3360459592871718290"><br/><i> <b>WOOOOHA, what a ride!! THE HEART OF BETRAYAL'S had me going on a ride of ups and downs like this...</b> </i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388194537ra/7763492.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <br/><i> <b>Because that was...</b> </i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426367696ra/14006975.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i> <b>And it left me feeling like this...</b> </i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426367452ra/14006958.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i> <b>But by the end of the book I was...</b> </i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426367452ra/14006959.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i> <b>This book was EPIC!! Truly, wonderfully EPICCC!!! I mean it was slow paced, especially in the beginning, but the first book was too. But that did NOTHING but strengthen this book! And that's weird because I usually HAVE to have a fast paced book for me to love it. But not with this series. AND YOU ARE</b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText3360459592871718290" style="display:none"><br><i> <b>WOOOOHA, what a ride!! THE HEART OF BETRAYAL'S had me going on a ride of ups and downs like this...</b> </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388194537ra/7763492.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><i> <b>Because that was...</b> </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426367696ra/14006975.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> <b>And it left me feeling like this...</b> </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426367452ra/14006958.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> <b>But by the end of the book I was...</b> </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426367452ra/14006959.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> <b>This book was EPIC!! Truly, wonderfully EPICCC!!! I mean it was slow paced, especially in the beginning, but the first book was too. But that did NOTHING but strengthen this book! And that's weird because I usually HAVE to have a fast paced book for me to love it. But not with this series. AND YOU ARE FAIR WARNED: THE ENDING IS TORTURE!!! HEARTBREAKING TORTURE!!! Man I have NO IDEA HOW I WILL WAIT A WHOLE YEAR UNTIL BOOK THREE IS IN MY NEEDY LITTLE HANDS....</b> </i><br><br><i> <b>~~~~~~~EDITED~~~~~~~</b> </i><br><br><br><i> <b>4.5 STARS</b> </i><br><br>A broken world built on bitter deception, ultimate betrayals, kindest friendships, faithful loyalties, sweet romance, unbreakable love, and the most deserving murders... THE HEART OF BETRAYAL will capture your heart and soul, and leave you breathless and utterly satisfied, but still craving more!!!<br><br>I don't even know where to begin to express my love for this book—series!! It's breathtaking, and the betrayals and revelations were beyond shocking and utterly heart wrenching to endure. At one point my heart became so entangled in where and who my loyalties lie with, that I wanted to scream at Pearson for creating such a flawless book, with brilliant character developments, and stunning chemistry, that I wanted Lia with BOTH of her love interest. Even though I knew it couldn't happen, but there were still moments in which I said, "Why-CAN'T-SHE-HAVE-THEM-BOTH???? WHY??????" And then I came back to my sense and was all #Team_Rafe again. BUT... I have to shamelessly admit after seeing Kaden in a new light, my love has grown tenfold for him in this book. And who knows, maybe by the end of the next book my loyalties could have easily switched to Kaden. And I have a gnawing feeling it's going to be an all out war choosing where and who I ultimately stand with at the end of this series. I just hope Pearson doesn't kill of one of the love interest. That would shatter my heart and make me beyond furious. But I don't think she'd take the easy out like that, at least I hope not!?!?!?!?!?!?!?!?!<br><br><i> <b>LIA:</b> </i><br><br>Lia is one of the best female protagonist I've ever read! And like the other characters in this book her character development is tremendous from the first book, yet with just the right amount of imperfections to make her realistic, yet flawed. And though she is a prisoner of Venda, she's still able to turn the wheel and grip control from time to time—enough that sometimes it's the only reason she's able to survive. Lia's intelligent, cunning, manipulative, and so determined to make it out of Venda with the one she loves, no matter the consequences she has to endure. But she's also kind-hearted, compassionate, understanding, helpful to those in need, and willing to stand up for those who can't. Now all those qualities combined make Lia a deadly combination—A force not to be reckoned with. And the girl is totally badass with a wooden sword, and even lethal with a steel one...<br><br><i> <b>RAFE:</b> </i><br><br>Rafe, where do I even begin to tell you how awesome he is? But at the same time I felt sorry for him, and the things he had to endure and do in order to keep his true motives and identity a secret. For that reason his character had many rolls in this book. He couldn't be the strong, determined, unwavering Prince, solider, and lover that he is. No, he had to suppress himself and bury his true inner being from all of Venda, because if his true identity was ever revealed, he would be going home pieces at a time, and Lia would be left in Venda, at the mercy of the Komizar, and that is something Rafe cannot let happen. I loved Rafe's patience's and self control over the situation he was in. He had to watch and endure much to conceal his identity, and it was slowly killing him, but he proved that he could endure the unthinkable for the chance to save the one he loved. And that made me love his character so much more then before. And I think the next book will mostly be in Dalbreck, and I'm hoping we'll finally get to see the REAL Rafe, and I cannot WAIT!!!<br><br><i> <b>KADEN:</b> </i><br><br>Kaden has tremendously grown on me in this book. So much in fact that I absolutely LOVE his character. He's bruised, and scarred, and blinded by his vengeance's. But he's also grown so much in this book too, and watching him go through the motions was moving, and made me understand him so much more, and his reasoning behind why he did/does the things that have accrued in his path. And for him Lia was the turning point that allowed him to view things differently. So much in fact that his love for her was evident to everyone in Venda, but sometimes was a blinding rage that consumed him. Lia is utterly Kaden's downfall, but also his savior... And I'm really curious to see what will happen between him and Lia in the next book. And for most of this book I was divided where my loyalties lie, Rafe or Kaden. But at the end of this book it was obvious where my heart lie, #TEAM_RAFE ALL THE WAY!!! But Kaden still holds a big part of my heart too. So we shall see if book three is the turning point for my ultimate love and loyalties! ;)<br><br><i> <b>THE PLOT</b> </i><br><br>Betrayed, captured, and kidnapped by the assassin Kaden, Lia is dragged hundreds of miles by Kaden's group of blood-thirsty Vendan's, and forcefully taken to the barbarian City of Venda, where she will have to convince the ruling Komizar that she is worth much more keeping alive then dead. If not, she may have to do the unthinkable to stay alive...<br><br>After enduring a harrowing journey, and watching someone she desperately loved murdered before her eyes, Lia thought it couldn't possibly get anymore complicated then this, but boy was she wrong. It's about to become a raging battle for survival, but not with weapons or fist. No, to beat this viciously cruel Komizar at his own game, Lia will have to become the ultimate weapon, and use not only her body and mind, but also every ounce of strength and skill she possesses, if she has any chance of escaping Venda alive. But first, she will have to become the enemy, to beat her enemy...<br><br>Being forced into enemy territory is not at all what Lia anticipated. After a horrific and challenging few weeks, Lia has endured much, but she is finally welcomed by a highly respected Vendan Clan, and gains support and privilege faster then she ever imagined. But that power also comes with it's own price. A price she's not sure she can pay?<br><br>But how can Lia possibly betray the same people who welcomed and believed in her? How can she crush the only fervor they've had in such a long time? But there is also one thing she cannot forget no matter how welcomed she thinks she is. She is still a prisoner of Venda, and no matter how good they treat her, or how much they put their faith in her, one way or another, she will pay for their generosity, even if it's with her body, or even her life...<br><br>Things become even more distressing when Rafe shows up and puts everything on the line, and gives Lia a reason to keep fighting. But Rafe also brings a hope with him that she thought was lost. A faith that help is on the way, that four of his most faithful and skilled soldiers are coming to aid in their escape. Even if it's only six people against thousands, Lia is still determined to keep fighting, even when it seems like an unbeatable battle.<br><br>Lia's world is an uproar of chaos and destruction, as her new life collides with her growing gift that unleashes when least suspected, her new roll in Venda, and the Komizar's threat that hangs in the balance. But even more unnerving is the ongoing weight that something more sinister is brewing in Venda, something that could even shatter all the kingdoms combined. Topped with her unwavering concealed deep affection for Rafe, Prince of Dalbreck, and her confusing relationship with the assassin Kaden, the supposed enemy. Lia's life has gone from bad to extremely deadly in a matter of weeks, and all she can do is bide her time and wait until the moment comes to strike, and strike she will, even if she has to kill for it...<br><br>My love for this book and series runs deep. I loved just about everything about these driven characters and broken world on the brink of war. I cannot think of any serious reason not to love this book as much as I do. Only thing I can say that was any bother whatsoever was the pacing and lack of steady action. It wasn't as fast paced as I would of liked, and at times felt like it dragged on some parts. The first book was like that too, and I think (I can't really remember) that's why I gave book one four stars and not the five I really wanted too. And their also wasn't really that much action. But even with the slow pace and unsteady flow of action, it didn't slow down my racing heart or gnawing desire for vengeance against all who wronged Lia. Or the sweet awe every time Rafe and Lia had stolen kisses hidden deep within the sanctum, or the complete and utter bliss when THE HEART OF BETRAYAL came to an end, or the fierce need for book three when the last words were read!! So even with it's minor flaws, I still very much loved this book and would get lost in it over and over again. Matter of fact, I'm rereading it now for my second time as I write this review. If that isn't love for a book then I don't know what is! ;)<br><br>Overall, THE HEART OF BETRAYAL was everything I thought it would be and some! I loved the beauty and horrific history in which this world was built upon, the exquisite culture and the remembrances that were created and brought to life, the fierce devotion in which our characters were willing to endure the unthinkable to fight for what they believed in. I could sit here all day naming the many reasons why I loved this book and thought it was the best. But theirs only three words I can think of that would do it any justice...<br><br><i> <b>UNTOUCHABLE, UNSTOPPABLE, AND INCOMPARABLE...</b> </i><br><br>P.S. And by the gods help me when book three, THE BEAUTY OF DARKNESS releases!!! OMG, I am going to shatter into a million pieces when that LONG, TORTUROUS, wait finally puts that EPIC book in my needy little hands!! Come on Pearson, give us that EXPLOSIVE ending that we're all craving!! So yeah, I think it's safe to say I absolutely loved this book,<br><br><i> <b>SO FREAKING HARD!!!! ;)</b> </i><br><br><i> <b>NOTE: I received a physical ARC from Henry Holt (Macmillan) for reviewing purposes! All opinions expressed are my own and are not influenced in any way!</b> </i><br><br><br></span>
